../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-16.txt:   pop culture. That leads us to the question, why are Arthurian legends

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-16.txt-   characters. For instance, BBC’s Merlin series and 1974 French drama
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-16.txt:   Lancelot du Lac. Many characters in Arthurian legends represent beloved

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-16.txt-   life and manages to ensure peace while he remains King. Archetypes can

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   Urban legends (sometimes modern legend, urban myth, or simply legend)
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   is a genre of folklore concerning stories about an unusual (usually
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   These legends can be entertaining but often concern mysterious peril or
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   troubling events, such as disappearances and strange objects or
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   entities. Urban legends may confirm moral standards, reflect
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   prejudices, or be a way to make sense of societal anxieties.^[2]
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   In the past, urban legends were most often circulated orally, at
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   gatherings and around the campfire for instance. Now, they can be
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   spread by any media, including newspapers, mobile news apps, e-mail,
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   and most often, social media. Some urban legends have passed through
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   the years/decades with only minor changes, in where the time period
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   takes place. Generic urban legends are often altered to suit regional
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   variations, but the lesson or moral generally remains the same.
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   The term "urban legend", as used by folklorists, has appeared in print
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   since at least 1968, when it was used by Richard Dorson.^[3] Jan Harold
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   the term to the general public in a series of popular books published
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   beginning in 1981. Brunvand used his collection of legends, The
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   Vanishing Hitchhiker: American Urban Legends & Their Meanings (1981) to
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   make two points: first, that legends and folklore do not occur
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   exclusively in so-called primitive or traditional societies, and
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   Many urban legends are framed as complete stories with plot and
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   characters. The compelling appeal of a typical urban legend is its
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   elements of mystery, horror, fear, or humor. Often they serve as
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   cautionary tales.^[5] Some urban legends are morality tales that depict
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   someone acting in a disagreeable manner, only to wind up in trouble,
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   Urban legends will often try to invoke a feeling of disgust in the
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   reader which tends to make these stories more memorable and potent.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   Elements of shock value can be found in almost every form of urban
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   legend and are partially what makes these tales so impactful.^[7] An
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   urban legend may include elements of the supernatural or
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   paranormal.^[8]
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   As Jan Brunvand points out,^[9] antecedent legends including some of
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   the motifs, themes and symbolism of the urtexts can readily be

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt-   enhance the power of the narrative^[14] while distancing the teller
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-1.txt:   from the tall tale. Many urban legends depict horrific crimes,

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-21.txt:   Legend displays. I set it to 60px and only the legend was showing. I

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:matplotlib.legend#
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   The legend module defines the Legend class, which is responsible for
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   drawing legends associated with Axes and/or figures.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   It is unlikely that you would ever create a Legend instance manually.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   Most users would normally create a legend via the legend function. For
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   more details on legends there is also a legend guide.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   The Legend class is a container of legend handles and legend texts.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   The legend handler map specifies how to create legend handles from
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   artists (lines, patches, etc.) in the Axes or figures. Default legend
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-   handlers are defined in the legend_handler module. While not all artist
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   types are covered by the default legend handlers, custom legend
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-   handlers can be defined to support arbitrary objects.
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:   class matplotlib.legend.DraggableLegend(legend, use_blit=False,

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      (default: 'best') for Axes, 'upper right' for Figure
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      The location of the legend.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      The strings 'upper left', 'upper right', 'lower
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      left', 'lower right' place the legend at the
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      corresponding corner of the axes/figure.

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      The strings 'upper center', 'lower center', 'center
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      left', 'center right' place the legend at the center
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      of the corresponding edge of the axes/figure.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      The string 'center' places the legend at the center
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      of the axes/figure.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      The string 'best' places the legend at the location,
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      among the nine locations defined so far, with the
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      The location can also be a 2-tuple giving the
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      coordinates of the lower-left corner of the legend
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      in axes/figure coordinates (in which case
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      There is ambiguity at the corners, so 'outside upper
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      right' will make space for the legend above the rest
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      of the axes in the layout, and 'outside right upper'
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      'outside left upper', and 'outside left lower'. See
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      Legend guide for more details.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-              bbox_to_anchorBboxBase, 2-tuple, or 4-tuple of floats
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      Box that is used to position the legend in
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt-                      conjunction with loc. Defaults to axes.bbox (if
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-23.txt:                      called as a method to Axes.legend) or figure.bbox

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:Legend
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   Genre of storytelling that involves heroic humans
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   For other uses, see Legend (disambiguation).
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   [220px-Lady_Godiva_%28John_Collier%2C_c._1897%29.jpg] In this 1897
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   painting of Lady Godiva by John Collier, the authentic historical
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   person is fully submerged in the legend, presented in an anachronistic
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   high medieval setting.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   A legend is a genre of folklore that consists of a narrative featuring
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   human actions, believed or perceived to have taken place in human
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   history. Narratives in this genre may demonstrate human values, and
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   possess certain qualities that give the tale verisimilitude. Legend,
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   for its active and passive participants, may include miracles. Legends
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   may be transformed over time to keep them fresh and vital.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   Many legends operate within the realm of uncertainty, never being
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   entirely believed by the participants, but also never being resolutely
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   doubted.^[1] Legends are sometimes distinguished from myths in that
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   they concern human beings as the main characters and do not necessarily
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   historical basis whereas myths generally do not.^[2]^[3] The Brothers
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   Grimm defined legend as "folktale historically grounded".^[4] A
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   by-product of the "concern with human beings" is the long list of
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   legendary creatures, leaving no "resolute doubt" that legends are
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   "historically grounded."
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   A modern folklorist's professional definition of legend was proposed by
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   Timothy R. Tangherlini in 1990:^[5]
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:     Legend, typically, is a short (mono-) episodic, traditional, highly
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-     ecotypified^[6] historicized narrative performed in a conversational
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   Legend is a loanword from Old French that entered English usage c.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   1340. The Old French noun legende derives from the Medieval Latin
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   (introduced in the 1510s) meaning a collection or corpus of
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   legends.^[8]^[9] This word changed to legendry, and legendary became
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   the adjectival form.^[8]
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   acknowledged in John Foxe's Actes and Monuments) was fictitious. Thus,
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   legend gained its modern connotations of "undocumented" and "spurious",
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-   which distinguish it from the meaning of chronicle.^[10]
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt-
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-2.txt:   In 1866, Jacob Grimm described the fairy tale as "poetic, legend

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            Jenna Taylor

../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            faceless man who lurks in the dark, the story of a man waking
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            up with a missing kidney — urban legends have always been
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            whispered to us. From a young age, we have been told stories
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            babysitter and hundreds of other stories that make our skin
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            crawl. Urban legends surround us, and they can be anything
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            from tales told on the school bus to internet stories. But why
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            much?
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            The term “urban legend” has been popular since the 1980s, when
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            Jan Harold Brunvand published his collection of urban legends
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            and their meanings. When discussing the story of the vanishing
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            hitchhiker, Harold wrote that the legend had evolved from
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            older European stories about travelers riding horseback. With
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            and wide, spreading by word of mouth to ears all around.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            Urban legends typically grow popular through storytelling. The
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            speaker usually claims that such things happened to “a friend
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            Because why would a friend lie? The peculiarities and suspense
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            of an urban legend are what makes them spread. The more
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            shocking yet realistic the story, the more we want to share
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            it. Sometimes, urban legends are told to extend caution and
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            sometimes, most times, they are simply good stories. Nowadays,
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            instant communication has made it easier for urban legends to
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            spread. For a long time, urban legend email chains were
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            popular, and now such tales are told on social media with a
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            their feeds.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            What makes urban legends so captivating is that they contain
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            elements from everyday life, such as walking through the
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            possibility that ordinary things could expose us to the
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            terrors these legends speak of. As time passes, urban legends
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            shift, retelling a modernized version of the story to newer
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            audiences, making urban legends everlasting.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            Some stories we take more seriously than others because apart
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            from entertainment, urban legends allow us to spread awareness
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            and preach caution about the dangers hidden in everyday life.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            But there have been times when urban legends have been taken
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            too seriously.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            In 2014, two girls attempted to brutally murder their best
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            friend because of the urban legend of the Slender Man. The
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            first time the name touched screens was in 2009, when two
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            It is important to be cautious when spreading stories,
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            especially among children. Because urban legends like this one
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            can quickly unfold into more elaborate, creative stories, our
--
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            not susceptible to becoming violent because of a story, urban
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            legends can trigger deep, dark fears, impacting us deeply and
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            oftentimes making us paranoid.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            Most people have been impacted by urban legends in one way or
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            another, whether that be hearing a story and sharing it with a
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            friend or stumbling upon a Creepypasta and not being able to
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            sleep in the dark for days. Urban legends are not typical
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            scary stories; they are spread with the notion that they are
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            true and that they are something we should beware of. Urban
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            legends must be spread with warning, as they can unravel more
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            than we know.
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            Urban legends can form innocently, sometimes with the simple
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            intention of amusing friends and sometimes with the intention
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            of evoking harmless fear. But as humans, we have a knack for
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt:            taking scary stories and legends too seriously. Do not believe
../dumps-text/anglais/anglais-30.txt-            everything you hear, and remember to spread stories with
